  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3d0b3f63-36cb-4e3a-9b01-1fb7b94f0250'
      });

<div id="review_2088055144" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2088055144" />
    <a title="Lena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50946393-lena"><img alt="Lena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483045416p2/50946393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2088055144?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lena" href="/user/show/50946393-lena">Lena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2088055144&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2088055144" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9122573216803076646">I don't understand how someone can continue to build completely new and fascinating worlds for the third time.<br/><br/>Wow, like, wow. I loved the whole Hives thing and the mysterious Tree Wars and the interesting set up of like, SilkWings under HiveWings and like the commentary on bystanders in a genocide (of trees) and generally like <br/><br/>aljdfhalksjd this ^ is what happens when I try to be sophisticated and coherent<br/><br/>okay so like, basically, i really liked it. my favorite thing about the first arc was like, </span>
  <span id="freeText9122573216803076646" style="display:none">I don't understand how someone can continue to build completely new and fascinating worlds for the third time.<br /><br />Wow, like, wow. I loved the whole Hives thing and the mysterious Tree Wars and the interesting set up of like, SilkWings under HiveWings and like the commentary on bystanders in a genocide (of trees) and generally like <br /><br />aljdfhalksjd this ^ is what happens when I try to be sophisticated and coherent<br /><br />okay so like, basically, i really liked it. my favorite thing about the first arc was like, discovering pyrrhia (spelling?) and all of the different kingdoms and the different cultures. each kingdom was unique and interesting and felt so well-developed for whatever part of the story they showed up in. it felt so adventurey and fun<br /><br />the second arc was only okay in that sense because the first book of it was literally just Moon going to school in a place we sort of already know and then we didn't get to explore more of the continent (other than the Ice Kingdom heck yeah)<br /><br />but this third arc, it's kind of a given that we would explore it since it's a WHOLE NEW CONTINENT<br /><br />im just saying, i loved the idea of the Hives and the wingless SilkWings till like, Metamorphosis and the one Queen ruling over two tribes. SilkWings being subservient to HiveWings and thoughts like "would these HiveWing guards still be nice if they were talking to a SilkWing?" and just akjdfhakj<br /><br />(subtle things like wood being a commodity because they CUT DOWN ALL OF THE TREES)<br /><br />(i have so many thoughts and no way of expressing them clearly)<br /><br />let me just say that i LOVE Blue, like a lot. he's great. he's kind of like a mix between Sunny and Turtle wherein he's really empathetic (in the beginning, he talks about how he likes to imagine himself as other dragons to see what it would be like to be them and throughout the book, whenever they're about to attack a HiveWing or something, he would say "what if he's having a bad day?" or "what if she has a family and she'll get in trouble if we leave her behind" and stuff like that, it was really sweet) and how he's also afraid of change and generally afraid to break the rules, and thus is very timid<br /><br />i loved his character arc, too, going from like always following the rules and believing that following the rules that would protect him to seeing that some rules are unjust and he needed to save his fellow SilkWings more importantly. when he meets his dad, it's kind of like seeing Blue again from the start of the book, where Admiral believes following the rules and writing letters to the queen would be more beneficial to the flamesilks, and even trying to turn in his own children to the guards when they try to escape. twas a nice way to showcase Blue's growth i feel<br /><br />also, i loved the general like discussion of following the rules and when to break them and when they were just and unjust. especially that one scene between Cricket and Blue when they agreed that one rule they should follow is "don't kill other dragons" but one they should not follow is "giving Queen Wasp whatever she wants" because it would harm the SilkWings. it was nice seeing that rule follow is like a gray area because some rules are unfair and some things are more important than following rules (like saving your sister from a lifetime of slavery, for instance) and that commentary continued throughout the whole book<br /><br />i don't know what im saying at this point, other than the fact that this is a very well written, funny, and complex middle grade series and it's fantastic<br /><br />im gonna stop talking now because i don't know what to say anymore<br /><br />i mean, other than the fact that i think this whole series is fantastic and everyone should read it<br /><br />uh, also that i spoiled a lot of stuff sort of<br /><br />maybe not<br /><br />i'll mark it for spoilers anyway</span>
  <a data-text-id="9122573216803076646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781338214437" href="/book/show/36127427-the-lost-continent">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22027176-connor?shelf=middle-grade-high-fantasy">middle-grade-high-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2268193855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11914278894584691175">So wow, I'm really loving all the new things introduced in their next arc of the Wings of Fire series. This one takes place at the same time as the tenth book, and I definitely don't recommend trying to jump into the series here. You should definitely go back and read from the beginning. I also highly suggest you read the prequel, Darkstalker before you read this one. <br/><br/>Now with that out of the way, I loved the new types of dragons brought into our journey through the world of Wings of Fire. They'</span>
  <span id="freeText11914278894584691175" style="display:none">So wow, I'm really loving all the new things introduced in their next arc of the Wings of Fire series. This one takes place at the same time as the tenth book, and I definitely don't recommend trying to jump into the series here. You should definitely go back and read from the beginning. I also highly suggest you read the prequel, Darkstalker before you read this one. <br /><br />Now with that out of the way, I loved the new types of dragons brought into our journey through the world of Wings of Fire. They're all so cool and unique. I thought how we got the history of this Lost Continent was really well done, and you can see how over time the dynamics between the different types of dragons shifted and evolved along with the environment of the continent itself. I liked the characters a lot. Blue was sooo frustrating, but that's just how he is. I thought he went through a lot of growth in this physically and mentally which was awesome to see. Luna was a great sister character pushing Blue but not too hard. Cricket was a fun, eccentric character that asks all the questions I had while reading! I really liked all of the other characters as well, and Sundew actually made me laugh out loud as I was listening to the audiobook. <br /><br />There is some instalove in this which was kind of annoying, but I appreciated that the novel was self aware about it and kind of pokes fun of it using other characters. I'm pretty excited to see how the new dragonets will handle their situations going forward, because this new arc promises some awesome rebellion and personal growth.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11914278894584691175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Allegra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77175824-allegra"><img alt="Allegra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528145161p2/77175824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2438694818?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allegra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allegra" href="/user/show/77175824-allegra">Allegra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781338214437" href="/book/show/36127427-the-lost-continent">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2438694818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6916296336521394330">It was wonderful coming back to the series through fresh eyes. I certainly had fun exploring the world, as well as the new dragons, set up by the author. It was the best course of action to focus on three species of dragons in this new world as opposed to the six that were in the previous books, especially if we are going to bring the two continents together as hinted at in the end of the last book as well as the end of this book. <br/>This series follows the wonderful pacing of the previous books, s</span>
  <span id="freeText6916296336521394330" style="display:none">It was wonderful coming back to the series through fresh eyes. I certainly had fun exploring the world, as well as the new dragons, set up by the author. It was the best course of action to focus on three species of dragons in this new world as opposed to the six that were in the previous books, especially if we are going to bring the two continents together as hinted at in the end of the last book as well as the end of this book. <br />This series follows the wonderful pacing of the previous books, starting at a calm but curious beginning and immediately throwing you into the action. I certainly was never bored while reading the book. The characters were each unique in personality and I can tell that the author is trying to branch out their appearances to match their personalities! <br />I would say the only down side would be the protagonist. That doesn't seem like a good thing but I would say this critique is that the protagonist has a loose personality. We have the main things established for Blue: He follows rules, he doesn't want to fight and cause a scene, etc. but other than that we don't see until later how his personality falls in line with his belief (the author tries to make "following the rules" a personality but it isn't). I enjoyed seeing his character slowly coming into picture but I only wish that it was clear from the beginning so we could follow his growth better. This could also apply to the other characters but not as much.<br />I would certainly recommend this book (I already have) because it is so much fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6916296336521394330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Annie (Putt)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47291796-annie-putt"><img alt="Annie (Putt)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582160152p2/47291796.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2475441039?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie (Putt)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie (Putt)" href="/user/show/47291796-annie-putt">Annie (Putt)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2475441039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6415859717479925500">4.5 stars<br/>Rereading definitely made me appreciate the world of The Lost Continent even more than the first time. The relationship between the SilkWings and HiveWings is so utterly heartbreaking. Queen Wasp's usage of a pacifistic society is sickening and a little too realistic, in some ways. SilkWings are raised with good food and homes and education, but they are forced into breeding programs (nothing as inhumane as warehouses or sex slaves, but they are told whom they can be mated with and so o</span>
  <span id="freeText6415859717479925500" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br />Rereading definitely made me appreciate the world of The Lost Continent even more than the first time. The relationship between the SilkWings and HiveWings is so utterly heartbreaking. Queen Wasp's usage of a pacifistic society is sickening and a little too realistic, in some ways. SilkWings are raised with good food and homes and education, but they are forced into breeding programs (nothing as inhumane as warehouses or sex slaves, but they are told whom they can be mated with and so on), trained for specific jobs and only those jobs, seen as second class citizens, and dissension and "misbehavior" is dealt with severely. Young SilkWings are taken every school year to the jail and forced to see what will happen if they misbehave. SilkWings who mature into flamesilks are thrown into dark pits and forced to spin their silk as a commodity for the HiveWings, controlled entirely by Queen Wasp. The dank caves with timed feeding is considered preferable by its inhabitants because, as Admiral tells Blue near the end of the book, "there used to be chains."<br /><br />This easy manipulation of power by Wasp and the devotion of the HiveWings--who unknowingly are pawns to Wasp as well--makes her one of the most interesting villains to date. Everything about this book makes me think about if Blister had become queen of the SandWings in the first series cycle. This is the series of "what happens after the evil queen wins the throne." I cannot wait to see how this plays out over the next four books. I find the characters to be fascinating, complex--though still needing development--and I want to learn more about Wasp, the war, and the geography of the continent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6415859717479925500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16613228601017342645">I've read all the Wings of Fire books from day one. And let me just say, this one is heckin' good. <br/><br/>Sutherland out did herself with world building by far. The new society and lore and how it ties into knowledge already established is mind blowing and makes you rethink everything you know about the series. <br/><br/>The characters are refreshing and original, and for an 11 soon to be 15 book series that's an impressive feat. It also establishes a main plot, and several plots for that matter, perfectly. And </span>
  <span id="freeText16613228601017342645" style="display:none">I've read all the Wings of Fire books from day one. And let me just say, this one is heckin' good. <br /><br />Sutherland out did herself with world building by far. The new society and lore and how it ties into knowledge already established is mind blowing and makes you rethink everything you know about the series. <br /><br />The characters are refreshing and original, and for an 11 soon to be 15 book series that's an impressive feat. It also establishes a main plot, and several plots for that matter, perfectly. And throughout this the writing style remains simple and easy to digest. <br /><br />But my favorite part were the themes. The Lost Continent deals with many strikingly relevant topics and themes in an honest yet brutal way that I couldn't help but appreciate. This is book is definitely a thrilling adventure, don't miss out on it! <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2285424136" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2285424136" />
    <a title="Ms. Yingling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2636606-ms-yingling"><img alt="Ms. Yingling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376174508p2/2636606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2285424136?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Yingling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Yingling" href="/user/show/2636606-ms-yingling">Ms. Yingling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781338214437" href="/book/show/36127427-the-lost-continent">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2285424136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9596850789220693855">Copy provided by Young Adult Books Central<br/><br/>Blue and his sister Luna are very close to going through metamorphosis, after which they will be given jobs and have a very different life. Blue is a rule follower and thinks that his life in Pantala is pretty good. Sure, it would be nice if the HiveWings were nicer and the SilkWings had more freedom, and if his father hadn't disappeared right after his birth, but those are minor issues compared to safety and order. When Luna starts to feel poorly while </span>
  <span id="freeText9596850789220693855" style="display:none">Copy provided by Young Adult Books Central<br /><br />Blue and his sister Luna are very close to going through metamorphosis, after which they will be given jobs and have a very different life. Blue is a rule follower and thinks that his life in Pantala is pretty good. Sure, it would be nice if the HiveWings were nicer and the SilkWings had more freedom, and if his father hadn't disappeared right after his birth, but those are minor issues compared to safety and order. When Luna starts to feel poorly while undergoing metamorphosis, the siblings realize it is because she is a very rare FlameSilk, which the HiveWings consider a dangerous threat and turn over to Queen Wasp. Blue, while he wants to do what he is told, thinks this is a bad plan, and tries to rescue his sister. Luckily, he runs into Cricket, a HiveWing who does not get sucked into the HiveWing mind when they are all told to capture Blue. Cricket is a quirky, talkative creature, and so interested in Blue that she's glad to help him out. Along with Swordtail, who loves Luna and whom the two rescue from the suspended animation he is held in as punishment, they head toward the home of the Queen Wasp to rescue Luna. They also run into a family of LeafWings, who are supposedly extinct, and they threaten to kill the dragonets unless they bring the Book of Clearsight back with them. With the help of their daughter, Sundew, Blue and Cricket venture deep into the lair of the HiveWings and their queen, find the librarian, who is in thrall to the wicked queen, manage to get the book, and find other secrets as well. Clearly, things won't be able to stay as they are, and as Blue approaches his metamorphosis, he knows that when he awakens, he will have a lot of work to do, work that might point him in the direction of the Lost Continent and other secrets that have been long suppressed in his society. <br /><br />While I am not a fan of long series involving different factions of dragons who all must fight the good fight, I can see the appeal of these books. My students are tremendously addicted to the Wings of Fire Series as well as the other series Sutherland helps to write, the Warrior Cats books. The arrival of the newest book is always a celebration. <br /><br />The characters are fun and spunky, and have delightful quirks that help readers root for them even when they are a little misguided. Blue's optimism in the face of completely unpleasant living conditions is rather charming, as is his constant battle with following rules when that means dragons he love might not be saved. Cricket, as an "evil" HiveWing shatters Blue's perceptions and endears herself to him by wanting to help him, asking relentless questions, and having secrets her own people don't understand, like growing an extinct tree in her class terrarium project! Swordtail's devotion is touching, and Luna's confusion and fear at undergoing a major change under less than optimal conditions is something which young readers will understand. <br /><br />The world building is also solid. My best friend in middle school was a huge fan of McCaffrey's Dragonriders of Pern, and was constantly going on and on about different facets of their world. The Lost Continent describes and defines and unique and well constructed dragon world, starting with a map of regions at the beginning, along with the back history of Clearsight and descriptions of the different kinds of dragons. These are the details that readers who want to submerge themselves in imaginary worlds crave, memorize, and endlessly repeat in conversations with other fans. <br /><br />There's plenty of adventure, traveling across the dragon world, danger, and occasional breaks for honey drops and other delicacies. This series is easier for me to follow than the Warriors, since there is generally a more defined quest centered on a main character with fewer supporting ones. Fans of Park's Wing and Claw series, Rocha's Secrets of Bearhaven and Kathryn Lasky's series like The Guardians of Ga'Hoole or Bears of the Ice will find this newest volume in the Wings of Fire series a worthy follow up to previous volumes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9596850789220693855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2597201978&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2597201978" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12204014270026623133">MORE dragons of such varying personalities, and I say that EVERY time, but it takes so much talent to write like that!<br/>New dragons on a new continent! And yet we still have things referenced back to what we know! <br/>It was so interesting to learn of these new dragons, and to explore their world and see how broken their tribes are!<br/>It was very interesting to read from the perspective of a dragon that doesn’t even have wings yet! <br/>Blue had such an interesting personality In that he always tried to think</span>
  <span id="freeText12204014270026623133" style="display:none">MORE dragons of such varying personalities, and I say that EVERY time, but it takes so much talent to write like that!<br />New dragons on a new continent! And yet we still have things referenced back to what we know! <br />It was so interesting to learn of these new dragons, and to explore their world and see how broken their tribes are!<br />It was very interesting to read from the perspective of a dragon that doesn’t even have wings yet! <br />Blue had such an interesting personality In that he always tried to think the best of everyone yet grew a lot by the end of the book. He always wanted to follow the rules, but then later realized he needed to do what was right, not necessarily what the rules said to do. <br />I’m so glad we got some insight on Clearsight, and that we got to see what happened to her after the events of Darkstalker. <br />The love between Cricket and Blue was also heartwarming and adorable! It’s also fascinating that Sutherland can write relationships fresh and different and new each time! They aren’t all the same. They don’t all just “love” each other, but they each have different reasons for their love or different outcomes etc. <br />However, basically everyone ends up with someone, which is not something I like in books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12204014270026623133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="GuineaPigFalconer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73657087-guineapigfalconer"><img alt="GuineaPigFalconer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510344418p2/73657087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2237523214?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="GuineaPigFalconer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="GuineaPigFalconer" href="/user/show/73657087-guineapigfalconer">GuineaPigFalconer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781338214437" href="/book/show/36127427-the-lost-continent">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2237523214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7449117895731851833">Before I started this book, I was a little worried that the series would start to get repetitive, as some do, but I should not have worried! This book follows new characters, on a new continent, with an entirely different way of life. Some of the subtle aspects of their culture are a bit dark and Big Brother-ish, which I found quite interesting, and something I wouldn't have expected from this series. The legends surrounding Clearsight were interesting, too. <br/>The characters were funny, adorable, </span>
  <span id="freeText7449117895731851833" style="display:none">Before I started this book, I was a little worried that the series would start to get repetitive, as some do, but I should not have worried! This book follows new characters, on a new continent, with an entirely different way of life. Some of the subtle aspects of their culture are a bit dark and Big Brother-ish, which I found quite interesting, and something I wouldn't have expected from this series. The legends surrounding Clearsight were interesting, too. <br />The characters were funny, adorable, and lovable as the Wings of Fire characters often are. And towards the end, I noticed a bit of a friend group forming, much like in previous books in this series. <br />The epilogue, in my best attempt not to spoil anything, sort of ties up the loose ends between this new series and the end of the last one. Poor Moon, after all she's been through, it looks like she's about to be put through some stuff again. <br />Read this book! It was so very fast and fun to read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7449117895731851833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

They are yellow with black stripes and spots (From there descentdent, Clearsight) They can have vemonus bites and claws that paralyze their victims, and they have 4 wings. They have anttenas that can sense danger. They are wingless till age 6, and then they go through metamorhphis, which they get wings. They can also spin silk, and rarely some have FLAMESILK.<br /><br />LeafWings- Were thought to be extinict, but they aren't. Green dragons with gold flecks. They have 2 wings and some can have an unsual control over plants.<br /><br />I LOVED THIS BOOK!!!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2556090025&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2556090025" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6105909066410069839"> I have been waiting for this book for nearly a year on the edge of my seat. I thought I wouldn't be able to make it to the release date but I did. My family and I went to Barnes and Noble the day after it came out and I read it as soon as I got home, but I haven't wanted to write a review till now. Tui T. Sutherland has a talent when it comes to writing characters and the characters were what I enjoyed the most in this newest Wings Of Fire book. Blue's arc reminds me a lot of Clay's character a</span>
  <span id="freeText6105909066410069839" style="display:none"> I have been waiting for this book for nearly a year on the edge of my seat. I thought I wouldn't be able to make it to the release date but I did. My family and I went to Barnes and Noble the day after it came out and I read it as soon as I got home, but I haven't wanted to write a review till now. Tui T. Sutherland has a talent when it comes to writing characters and the characters were what I enjoyed the most in this newest Wings Of Fire book. Blue's arc reminds me a lot of Clay's character arc in The Dragonet Prophecy, both started out shy and wanting to avoid conflict as much as possible but by the end of his story he knows that he must fight to protect those he cares about. Swordtail was a good character to keep a variety in our new group of heroes but the dragon that really stole the spotlight was our beloved Cricket. She is such a fun, enjoyable, and lovably crazy hivewing that you cant't help but fall in love with her energy that somehow blends perfectly with Blue's personality. On the other hand there are some small things included in the first Wings of Fire arc that Sutherland didn't add to this book most likely due to being rushed to finish it on time. She didn't mention small stuff like what do hivewings sound like when they fly, what is it like when silkwings fly, etc. In the first few books she brings up things like skywings fly incredibly fast at really high speeds. It wasn't obvious but I missed having that with this book. But in the end I absolutely loved this book, I had fun reading it, and the writing kept me on the edge of my seat until the very last page! I am very excited for the Hive Queen and I hope it is as good as some of my favorites so far in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6105909066410069839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10791665612660550581" style="display:none">This is the 11th book in the the Wings of Fire Series. You do not have to read the books prior to it because it is a new storyline. <br /><br />Blue, the young obedient silk wing dragon, goes on an adventure to save his sister Luna. These dragons are butterflies and wasps, they live in a hive instead of huts or caves like the previous series. Blue was caught in a situation where his sister’s metamorphosis day was disrupted by an unexpected problem and he is stuck in a dangerous situation with a dangerous plan. This is like all of the wings of fire books, because his friends are always there to help<br /><br />I like this book times a septillion, and recommend it to people who have read the other Wings Of Fire books, even if you only started the first WoF books because it is a good book, also recommend it to people who like dragons because there are a lot of new dragons.</span>

  <span id="freeText9182660074963004714" style="display:none">Thoughts: This book is the best in the series yet. When I started reading the first book in the third sub-series of Wings of Fire I expected it to be okay, however when I finished it was the best Wings of Fire book I've read yet. I love how Tui T. Sutherland used some attributes from past Wings of Fire characters to create new characters. For example, Cricket (one of the main characters) is a lot like Kinkajou form the past Wings of Fire books. Another thing that I enjoyed about The Lost Continent was all the new species of dragons. One of my favorite things about the Wings of Fire series is all the different dragons and powers. I was sad when Tui T. Sutherland had of the same powers and dragons in the first ten books, but I was really excited in book eleven with all the new dragons and powers. Overall, I love, love, love this fabulous, amazing, funny, creative book.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2304819672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8253430075318472527">Yay!!! New dragons!!! I love love love this series. Yes, they are written for kids but the writing style is flawless, the plots are deep and full of unexpected twists, and there is plenty of blood and romance to keep me entertained. Seriously, you guys should read this series. If you love fantasy at all, I think you'll like these books. I'm so excited to see what happens next to our new set of dragonets from the Lost Continent! Ten out of five stars to The Lost Continent!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Q015w5SXVAQ0mDRdXQMjUmGt5xDTXzUhJItYiU3/fJ2+ZMJBsUyK7rsOZ6rDOCg2/7xlkVdMujPyEzn6v4NH+g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uVMOg9JZ1FtLPMSVU4Jgh/TFF45Pa8NHzpmQq1gStUtEerUB94IKscSql2LNuWvjatSVD8t4TFUYAfHYqm6OLA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer959981775131074749">Okay, I know what you’re thinking. Tui? What kind of name is that? Is it short for something?<br/><br/>Nope. Among the many great things to come out of New Zealand (the Lord of the Rings movies, cats that paint, my mom) is a bird called the tui—not as well known as the kiwi, but a heck of a lot noisier!<br/><br/>I was born July 31 (same birthday as Harry Potter!) in Caracas, Venezuela, and lived in Asuncion, Paraguay</span>
  <span id="freeText959981775131074749" style="display:none">Okay, I know what you’re thinking. Tui? What kind of name is that? Is it short for something?<br /><br />Nope. Among the many great things to come out of New Zealand (the Lord of the Rings movies, cats that paint, my mom) is a bird called the tui—not as well known as the kiwi, but a heck of a lot noisier!<br /><br />I was born July 31 (same birthday as Harry Potter!) in Caracas, Venezuela, and lived in Asuncion, Paraguay; Miami, Florida; and Santo Domingo, Dominican Republic, before moving to New Jersey in high school, where I started doing theatre—mostly backstage work, because (a) it was fun, and (b) you got to hang out in the dark with cute boys. (Er, I mean . . . because it was artistically fulfilling, yes.)<br /><br />I graduated from Williams College in ’98 and I currently live in Boston with my husband, my perfect new baby, and my adorable yoodle Sunshine (what’s a yoodle? A puppy that’s three-quarters poodle and one-quarter Yorkshire terrier, of course!).<br /><br />Much to my parents’ relief, I abandoned my theatrical aspirations after college for the far more stable and lucrative career of fiction writing.<br /><br />My first two official books were beginning readers, part of Grosset &amp; Dunlap’s “First Friends” series for kids learning to read. MEET MO AND ELLA is tough to find now, but FUN WITH MO AND ELLA should still be out there somewhere.<br /><br />My first novel for teenagers was THIS MUST BE LOVE, which retells Shakespeare’s play A Midsummer Night’s Dream in a modern-day high school, from the POV of the two heroines, Hermia and Helena.<br /><br />And now I'm writing in a new project called SEEKERS! It's a children's book series that I'm writing with Erin Hunter. Check out my blog to find out more!</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/57525445-the-lost-continent">Quotes from The Lost Continent</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Oh, I’m not allowed to take art classes anymore,” Cricket said with a kind of carelessness he was pretty sure she was faking. “You can proooooobably guess why.” “Good heavens, Cricket,” he said, putting on the voice she’d used several times already. “No one has ever used that many colors on one piece of paper before. Look at this mess. Why can’t you just draw a normal blue blueberry like every other dragon?&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/10076365-oh-i-m-not-allowed-to-take-art-classes-anymore-cricket">3 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
